@Xoyaral Signing the exe is like signing a document: You slap your signature on it so you can prove it's yours. Microsoft is doing that with Windows applications: If it's not signed by MS, it will pop up that annoying message. So, to get MS's signature, you have to buy it. And that costs a fuck ton of money

[01-Mar-20 01:32 AM] LeafHacker#5373
Not 100% accurate; we'd never be able to sign anything with MS key, but we can get our own key and sign stuff. The hard/expensive part is getting our key listed by someone Microsoft trusts. That is usually a paid subscription.

[01-Mar-20 01:34 AM] LeafHacker#5373
(technically, our key would be split into private and public keys; the private key is used to sign stuff and the public key is used to verify the signature. The public key would be listed publicly by an "authority" that MS trusts and we pay, the private key would be top secret)

[01-Mar-20 01:34 AM] LeafHacker#5373
_my understanding_ is that if we did that then the security warning would probably go away.
